[[File:Ministro da Cultura do Congo (5654738321).jpg|thumb|Jean-Claude Gakosso with [[Jaques Wagner]] in 2011]]
-'''Jean-Claude Gakosso''' (born 25 July 1957{{webarchive |url=https://web.archive.org/web/20071221200920/http://www.congo-site.net/v4x/instit/gouvernement/minicult.php |date=December 21, 2007 |title=Page on Gakosso at Congo-site.net }} {{fr icon}}.) is a [[Republic of the Congo|Congolese]] politician who has served in the government of Congo-Brazzaville as Minister of Foreign Affairs since 2015. Previously he was Minister of Culture and the Arts from 2002 to 2015.
+'''Jean-Claude Gakosso''' (born 25 July 1957{{Wayback |date=20071221200920 |df=yes|url=http://www.congo-site.net/v4x/instit/gouvernement/minicult.php |title=Page on Gakosso at Congo-site.net }} {{fr icon}}.) is a [[Republic of the Congo|Congolese]] politician who has served in the government of Congo-Brazzaville as Minister of Foreign Affairs since 2015. Previously he was Minister of Culture and the Arts from 2002 to 2015.

==Professional and political career==
Gakosso, an ethnic [[Mbochi people|Mbochi]],Emmanuel Okamba, ''La gouvernance, une affaire de société: Analyse mythiumétrique de la performance'' (2010), page 181 {{fr icon}}. was born in [[Inkouélé]], located in the [[Gamboma District]] of [[Plateaux Region, Congo|Plateaux Region]], and studied at the [[University of Paris|Sorbonne]] in France. He was a lecturer on [[journalism]] at the [[Marien Ngouabi University]] in [[Brazzaville]], and in 1995 he criticized a press law passed by the [[National Assembly of the Republic of the Congo|National Assembly]], accusing the government of "working to restrict press freedom".Nana Rosine Ngangoue, [http://www.highbeam.com/doc/1P1-6234245.html "Congo-media: Muzzling the press"], Inter Press Service English News Wire, 30 September 1995. After the [[Republic of the Congo civil war|June–October 1997 civil war]], he was Adviser for Communication, Posts, and Telecommunications to President [[Denis Sassou Nguesso]] from 1997 to 2002."Who's Who", ''Congo Brazzaville: Les Hommes de Pouvoir'', number 1, [http://www.africaintelligence.fr Africa Intelligence], 29 October 2002 {{fr icon}}.

-On 18 August 2002, he was appointed to the government as Minister of Culture, Arts, and Tourism;[http://fr.allafrica.com/stories/200208210540.html "Le nouveau gouvernement a été mis en place"], ''La Semaine Africaine'', 22 August 2002 {{fr icon}}."La composition du nouveau gouvernement congolais", ''Les Dépêches de Brazzaville'', 19 August 2002 {{fr icon}}. {{webarchive |url=https://web.archive.org/web/20120528210822/http://www.brazzaville-adiac.com/index.php?action=depeche&dep_id=1420&oldaction=liste®pay_id=0&them_id=0&cat_id=0&ss_cat_id=0&LISTE_FROM=60&select_month=0&select_year=0 |date=May 28, 2012 }} he succeeded [[Mambou Aimée Gnali]] at the head of that ministry on 22 August.[http://www.brazzaville-adiac.com/index.php?action=depeche&dep_id=1459&oldaction=liste®pay_id=0&them_id=0&cat_id=0&ss_cat_id=0&LISTE_FROM=0&select_month=08&select_year=2002 "Jean-Claude Gakosso prend ses fonctions au ministère de la Culture, des arts et du tourisme"], ''Les Dépêches de Brazzaville'', 23 August 2002 {{fr icon}}.
+On 18 August 2002, he was appointed to the government as Minister of Culture, Arts, and Tourism;[http://fr.allafrica.com/stories/200208210540.html "Le nouveau gouvernement a été mis en place"], ''La Semaine Africaine'', 22 August 2002 {{fr icon}}."La composition du nouveau gouvernement congolais", ''Les Dépêches de Brazzaville'', 19 August 2002 {{fr icon}}. {{Wayback |date=20120528210822 |df=yes|url=http://www.brazzaville-adiac.com/index.php?action=depeche&dep_id=1420&oldaction=liste®pay_id=0&them_id=0&cat_id=0&ss_cat_id=0&LISTE_FROM=60&select_month=0&select_year=0}} he succeeded [[Mambou Aimée Gnali]] at the head of that ministry on 22 August.[http://www.brazzaville-adiac.com/index.php?action=depeche&dep_id=1459&oldaction=liste®pay_id=0&them_id=0&cat_id=0&ss_cat_id=0&LISTE_FROM=0&select_month=08&select_year=2002 "Jean-Claude Gakosso prend ses fonctions au ministère de la Culture, des arts et du tourisme"], ''Les Dépêches de Brazzaville'', 23 August 2002 {{fr icon}}.

In a ceremony at the [[Marien Ngouabi Mausoleum]], Gakosso rekindled the [[eternal flame]] commemorating President [[Marien Ngouabi]] on 11 November 2002. The flame had been extinguished since the 1997 war. Speaking on the occasion, Gakosso said that he had prioritized the restoration of the flame when he took over as Minister of Culture because "it symbolizes the pain, resistance, self-sacrifice, and courage embodied by President Marien Ngouabi."[http://www.brazzaville-adiac.com/index.php?action=depeche&dep_id=2082&oldaction=liste®pay_id=0&them_id=0&cat_id=0&ss_cat_id=0&LISTE_FROM=60&select_month=0&select_year=0 "Jean-Claude Gakosso ranime la flamme du mausolée Marien Ngouabi à Brazzaville"], ''Les Dépêches de Brazzaville'', 14 November 2002 {{fr icon}}. At the time of the fifth [[Panafrican Music Festival]] in Brazzaville in July 2005, Gakosso was President of the Festival's Steering Committee.David Cadasse, [http://www.afrik.com/article8628.html "Fespam 2005"], Afrik.com, 18 July 2005 {{fr icon}}.

===1964–65: Rise to fame===
[[File:Donovan (1965).jpg|thumb|left|Donovan (1965)]]
-Returning to [[Hatfield, Hertfordshire|Hatfield]], he spent several months playing in local clubs, absorbing the folk scene around his home in [[St Albans]], learning the [[Fingerpicking|crosspicking]] guitar technique from local players such as [[Mac MacLeod]] and [[Mick Softley]] and writing his first songs. In 1964, he travelled to [[Manchester]] with [[Gyp Mills|Gypsy Dave]], then spent the summer in [[Torquay]], Devon. In Torquay he stayed with Mac MacLeod and took up [[busking]], studying the guitar, and learning [[traditional music|traditional]] folk and blues.{{cite web|last=Dixon|first=Kevin|url=http://www.peoplesrepublicofsouthdevon.co.uk/2010/07/17/torquays-other-history-the-inspiration-of-folk-superstars-donovan-and-mac-macleod|title=Torquay's other history: the inspiration of folk superstars Donovan and Mac Macleod|publisher=Peoplesrepublicofsouthdevon.co.uk|date=17 July 2010|accessdate=18 May 2011}}{{webarchive |url=https://web.archive.org/web/20090430165209/http://www.macmacleod.co.uk/reviews.html |date=April 30, 2009 |title=reviews }}
+Returning to [[Hatfield, Hertfordshire|Hatfield]], he spent several months playing in local clubs, absorbing the folk scene around his home in [[St Albans]], learning the [[Fingerpicking|crosspicking]] guitar technique from local players such as [[Mac MacLeod]] and [[Mick Softley]] and writing his first songs. In 1964, he travelled to [[Manchester]] with [[Gyp Mills|Gypsy Dave]], then spent the summer in [[Torquay]], Devon. In Torquay he stayed with Mac MacLeod and took up [[busking]], studying the guitar, and learning [[traditional music|traditional]] folk and blues.{{cite web|last=Dixon|first=Kevin|url=http://www.peoplesrepublicofsouthdevon.co.uk/2010/07/17/torquays-other-history-the-inspiration-of-folk-superstars-donovan-and-mac-macleod|title=Torquay's other history: the inspiration of folk superstars Donovan and Mac Macleod|publisher=Peoplesrepublicofsouthdevon.co.uk|date=17 July 2010|accessdate=18 May 2011}}{{Wayback |df=yes|date=20090430165209 |url=http://www.macmacleod.co.uk/reviews.html |title=reviews}}

In late 1964, he was offered a management and publishing contract by [[Peter Eden]] and [[Geoff Stephens]] of [[Pye Records]] in London, for which he recorded a 10-track [[demo tape]] (later released on [[iTunes]]), which included the original of his first single, "[[Catch the Wind]]", and "[[Josie (Donovan song)|Josie]]". The first song revealed the influence of [[Woody Guthrie]] and [[Ramblin' Jack Elliott]], who had also influenced [[Bob Dylan]]. Dylan comparisons followed for some time.{{Gilliland|url=http://digital.library.unt.edu/ark:/67531/metadc19823/m1 |title=Show 48 – The British are Coming! The British are Coming!: With an emphasis on Donovan, the Bee Gees and the Who. [Part 5] |accessdate=18 May 2011}} In an interview with [[KFOK-LP|KFOK]] radio in the US on 14 June 2005, MacLeod said: "The press were fond of calling Donovan a Dylan clone as they had both been influenced by the same sources: Ramblin' Jack Elliott, [[Jesse Fuller]], Woody Guthrie, and many more."{{Citation needed|date=February 2013}}

{{main|Aberfan disaster}}
For many years, millions of cubic metres of excavated mining debris from the colliery were deposited on the side of [[Mynydd Merthyr]], directly above the village of Aberfan on the opposite side of the valley. Huge piles, or "tips", of loose rock and mining spoil had been built up over a layer of highly porous [[sandstone]] that contained numerous underground [[spring (hydrosphere)|spring]]s, and several tips had been built up directly over these springs. Although local authorities had raised specific concerns in 1963 about spoil being tipped on the mountain above the village primary school, these were largely ignored by the [[National Coal Board]]'s area management.{{cite web|url=http://www.nuffield.ox.ac.uk/politics/aberfan/letters.htm|title=Letters used as evidence by Tribunal of Inquiry|first=|last=martin|publisher=nuffield.ox.ac.uk|accessdate=21 October 2016}}

-Early on the morning of Friday, 21 October 1966, after several days of heavy rain, a subsidence of about 3–6 metres occurred on the upper flank of colliery waste tip No. 7. At 9:15 a.m. more than 150,000 cubic metres of water-saturated debris broke away and flowed downhill at high speed. A mass of over 40,000 cubic metres of debris slid into the village in a slurry {{convert|12|m}} deep.[http://www.south-wales.police.uk/fe/master.asp?n1=8&n2=253&n3=492 South Wales Police official website - The Aberfan Disaster] {{webarchive |url=https://web.archive.org/web/20090207190307/http://www.south-wales.police.uk/fe/master.asp?n1=8&n2=253&n3=492 |date=February 7, 2009 }}
+Early on the morning of Friday, 21 October 1966, after several days of heavy rain, a subsidence of about 3–6 metres occurred on the upper flank of colliery waste tip No. 7. At 9:15 a.m. more than 150,000 cubic metres of water-saturated debris broke away and flowed downhill at high speed. A mass of over 40,000 cubic metres of debris slid into the village in a slurry {{convert|12|m}} deep.[http://www.south-wales.police.uk/fe/master.asp?n1=8&n2=253&n3=492 South Wales Police official website - The Aberfan Disaster] {{wayback|df=yes|url=http://www.south-wales.police.uk/fe/master.asp?n1=8&n2=253&n3=492 |date=20090207190307 }}

The slide destroyed a farm and twenty terraced houses along Moy Road, and struck the northern side of the Pantglas Junior School and part of the separate senior school, demolishing most of the structures and filling the classrooms with thick mud and rubble up to {{convert|10|m}} deep. Mud and water from the slide flooded many other houses in the vicinity, forcing many villagers to evacuate their homes.

In September 2012 the centre ceased to be part of MK College and became a wholly owned subsidiary of the University of Bedfordshire.[http://www.beds.ac.uk/news/2012/april/university-college-milton-keynes-to-open-in-2012 'University College Milton Keynes’ to open in 2012] The university announced plans for a new campus in the city, with the new name of the institution being 'University Campus Milton Keynes', and this was opened at Saxon Court on Avebury Boulevard in September 2013.[http://www.bbc.co.uk/news/uk-england-beds-bucks-herts-21895773 New £25m university campus planned for Milton Keynes] - BBC[http://www.beds.ac.uk/news/2014/september/ucmk-celebrates-first-birthday UCMK celebrates first birthday]

==Academics==
-When it was part of MK College, the campus offered [[Higher National Certificate]]s, [[Higher National Diploma]]s, [[Foundation Degree]]s and the [[Professional Graduate Certificate in Education]] as programmes of study, as well as various management and professional courses. Whilst Milton Keynes College was the chief operator of UCMK, most higher education courses were accredited by the [[University of Bedfordshire]], with some courses accredited by the [[University of Northampton]], The [[Open University]] and [[Oxford Brookes University]].{{webarchive |url=https://web.archive.org/web/20111108220537/http://www.ucmk.ac.uk/courses/management-professional-courses |date=November 8, 2011 |title=Management & Professional Courses }}
+When it was part of MK College, the campus offered [[Higher National Certificate]]s, [[Higher National Diploma]]s, [[Foundation Degree]]s and the [[Professional Graduate Certificate in Education]] as programmes of study, as well as various management and professional courses. Whilst Milton Keynes College was the chief operator of UCMK, most higher education courses were accredited by the [[University of Bedfordshire]], with some courses accredited by the [[University of Northampton]], The [[Open University]] and [[Oxford Brookes University]].{{wayback|url=http://www.ucmk.ac.uk/courses/management-professional-courses|title=Management & Professional Courses|date=20111108220537|df=yes}}

Today, under the operation of the University of Bedfordshire, UCMK offers Foundation degrees, [[Bachelor's degree]]s and [[Master's degree]]s.http://www.ucmk.ac.uk/courses

{{Use British English|date=October 2016}}
'''Acen Razvi''' is a former early 1990s [[United Kingdom|UK]] [[rave music|rave]] and [[breakbeat hardcore]]/[[oldskool jungle|jungle]] producer. Acen was known for tracks such as "Close Your Eyes", "Window in the Sky" and "Trip II the Moon" (the latter two both 1992). He worked for the [[Production House Records]] stable,[http://www.discogs.com/label/Production+House Production House] which also brought fame to [[Baby D (dance group)|Baby D]]. He released the album ''75 Minutes''.[http://www.discogs.com/release/47477 Acen - 75 Minutes]

-He has also collaborated with [[Baby D (dance group)|Baby D]]'s Floyd Dice to form The House Crew.[http://www.discogs.com/artist/House+Crew%2C+The House Crew, The] {{webarchive |url=https://web.archive.org/web/20070823015945/http://www.discogs.com/artist/House+Crew%2C+The |date=August 23, 2007 }}
+He has also collaborated with [[Baby D (dance group)|Baby D]]'s Floyd Dice to form The House Crew.[http://www.discogs.com/artist/House+Crew%2C+The House Crew, The] {{wayback|df=yes|url=http://www.discogs.com/artist/House+Crew%2C+The |date=20070823015945 }}

He is now a filmmaker, specialising in short films under the name Acen Films Limited to be shown at festivals.{{citation needed|date=January 2012}} Besides producing dance music tracks, his aim is to fuse art forms and to introduce pioneering visual and musical perceptions to new audiences.{{citation needed|date=January 2012}}
